  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5f51be88-b46d-4b8a-afe4-5f235fac7026'
      });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_248642677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248642677" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248642677?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248642677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4190536218869197167">Well, finally after a series of disappointing sequels this year (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13042154.Rebel_Heart__Dust_Lands___2_' title='Rebel Heart (Dust Lands, #2) by Moira Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rebel Heart</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11735983.Insurgent__Divergent___2_' title='Insurgent (Divergent, #2) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Insurgent</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11765920.The_Calling__Darkness_Rising___2_' title='The Calling (Darkness Rising, #2) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Calling</a>) I've found a book that was even better than its predecessor. I think Rossi has gone even further with this installment, building on her characters and their relationships with one another, creating a number of funny, sad and ultimately memorable little moments that made me even more invested in the bigger picture. What she does best here is get the balance right between fast-paced action/adventu</span>
  <span id="freeText4190536218869197167" style="display:none">Well, finally after a series of disappointing sequels this year (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13042154.Rebel_Heart__Dust_Lands___2_" title="Rebel Heart (Dust Lands, #2) by Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel Heart</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11735983.Insurgent__Divergent___2_" title="Insurgent (Divergent, #2) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Insurgent</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11765920.The_Calling__Darkness_Rising___2_" title="The Calling (Darkness Rising, #2) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">The Calling</a>) I've found a book that was even better than its predecessor. I think Rossi has gone even further with this installment, building on her characters and their relationships with one another, creating a number of funny, sad and ultimately memorable little moments that made me even more invested in the bigger picture. What she does best here is get the balance right between fast-paced action/adventure scenes and character development, I now have no doubt in my mind as to whether I'll be reading the next book.<br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13253276.Through_the_Ever_Night__Under_the_Never_Sky___2_" title="Through the Ever Night (Under the Never Sky, #2) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Ever Night</a>, Perry and Aria face many challenges to their relationship and to their lives. Now that Perry is Blood Lord of the Tides, he carries all the responsibility for the welfare of his people and it turns out to be a very heavy burden. Not only that, but the Tides are not so ready to welcome Aria and some of them begin to question whether Perry is a suitable leader or too governed by his heart. Roar becomes an even more prominent character too (and possibly my favourite) and I really liked the way Rossi managed to successfully write a platonic and convincing relationship between male and female characters of roughly the same age - this doesn't happen too often unless the guy is the stereotypical "gay friend".<br><br>Another thing I noticed - and was a refreshing change to the genre - is that the author allows bad stuff to happen. What I mean by this is that the good guys don't always get what they want and sometimes things don't end with a happily ever after - I just appreciate this more realistic approach to storytelling. In real life, not everything works out for the good people and Rossi shows that here. <br><br>The funny thing is, that of all those sequels I was looking forward to, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13253276.Through_the_Ever_Night__Under_the_Never_Sky___2_" title="Through the Ever Night (Under the Never Sky, #2) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Ever Night</a> was the one I was anticipating the least for some reason. But this suspenseful, action-packed read was pretty fabulous, I don't think fans of the first will have anything to worry about because this sequel takes all the elements that we loved from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11594257.Under_the_Never_Sky__Under_the_Never_Sky___1_" title="Under the Never Sky (Under the Never Sky, #1) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Never Sky</a> and multiplies them by a hundred. I enjoyed it immensely and I can't imagine I will be forgetting the hilarious duet scene with Aria and Roar for a long while.<br><br><br><b>...........................................................................................................<br>Before reading:</b><br><br>Who is this dude and what has he done with Perry?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365190i/717070.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, firstly: <b><i>"His hair looked like it had never seen a brush. Snarled blond ropes, all uneven in length and color, coiling in every direction."</i> - pg 110</b> Um, so not only has he shopped at Abercrombie &amp; Fitch since the last book, he's also found time for a cut and dye job.<br><br>Secondly, this is totally not the Perry I was picturing after the first cover was: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365190i/717071.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All shirtless and wild hair and perhaps you can't just ask people this but I can't help myself so:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365190ra/717072.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4190536218869197167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <u>Fifth Time Read Review</u>

It has taught me so many things and it changed how I looked at myself, other people and the world and I think I learnt self-respect and self-love with the help of this trilogy. I’m forever grateful for the existence of this trilogy in this world. 💖<br><br>I also chose this trilogy to be analyzed for my upcoming thesis and wow. I am so freaking happy and nervous!     <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/448128503?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-arc">netgalley-edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=freaking-brilliant">freaking-brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=highly-anticipating-2013">highly-anticipating-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-need-this-book">i-need-this-book</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448128503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer511455034785826247"><b>
  <i>This review contains spoilers for Under the Never Sky.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Recently--and far too often, if you ask me--in young adult trilogies, second installments have been widely known to be practically a resting point for both the author, and the characters and the plot. Instead of what <i>should</i> be an intense ride setting up for the final installment, the second installment in a trilogy is, more often than not, a complete and utter bore ending with a bang to lure readers who were less than impressed with the s</span>
  <span id="freeText511455034785826247" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>This review contains spoilers for Under the Never Sky.</i>
</b><br /><br />Recently--and far too often, if you ask me--in young adult trilogies, second installments have been widely known to be practically a resting point for both the author, and the characters and the plot. Instead of what <i>should</i> be an intense ride setting up for the final installment, the second installment in a trilogy is, more often than not, a complete and utter bore ending with a bang to lure readers who were less than impressed with the second installment to come back and read the third. <br /><br />Clearly, Veronica Rossi did not receive the memo that apparently this is how second installments are treated nowadays, which is evident by the sheer awesomeness that is <i>Through the Ever Night</i>. <i>Through the Ever Night</i> takes place few months after the ending of <i>Under the Never Sky</i>; Perry is now the Blood Lord of the Tides, and is reunited with Aria after being departed for months. While Perry is dealing with his newfound duties and stresses that come with being the Blood Lord, Aria is still determined to find Perry's nephew, Talon, and bring him back to the Tides, all while having to worry about the monstrous Aether storms taunting her, Perry, and everyone else, above. <br /><br /><i>Through the Ever Night</i> was everything that <i>Under the Never Sky</i> was times ten--it was fast-paced, thrilling, full of action, full of character and relationship development, full of heartbreak, and full of Aether (lots and lots of Aether!). Every single thing that made <i>Under the Never Sky</i> amazing was in <i>Through the Ever Sky</i>, and somehow, Rossi managed to make those aspects even <i>more</i> amazing, adding more and more depth to them. <br /><br />One of my favorite things about the <i>Under the Never Sky trilogy</i> so far is the relationships and character dynamics that Veronica Rossi so masterly develops throughout the course of the novels. Aria has grown so much as a character since <i>Under the Never Sky</i>--both emotionally and physically--and the same goes for Perry, Roar, and a few other familiar faces. As well as the huge amount of character growth in the series thus far, the relationships and romance are absolutely brilliant. The romance between Perry and Aria will most likely end up being one of my favorites in young adult by the end of the trilogy, and the thing I have to say I love most about the romance in this trilogy is that, while it is certainly an important factor, it never overshadows other factors such as the plot--which appears to be another case of Rossi not receiving a memo most authors, unfortunately, have. The relationship between Aria and Roar, too, is absolutely one to praise, and is <i>definitely</i> one of my favorite relationships of the year, bearing one of the most interesting and heartwarming dynamics I've ever had the pleasure to read, and that's not just because I love Roar with a passion. The friendship these two characters have with each other, and the fact that you can just <i>feel</i> how much they care about each other seeping through the pages is certainly something special, as is the fact that you know their relationship will not ever cross into romantic territory--proving once <i>again</i> that Rossi must have missed a memo most authors have received, proving that some friends <i>can</i> remain just that--friends--and amazing ones at that. <br /><br />With all this glowing praise, I can say with complete and utter certainty that fans of <i>Under the Never Sky</i> will have just an amazing of a time with <i>Through the Ever Night</i> as I had, and I can even say that those who weren't fans of <i>Under the Never Sky</i> will most likely be impressed with <i>Through the Ever Night</i>. <i>Through the Ever Night</i> is hands down one of the most outstanding sequels I've ever had the pleasure to read, and I thoroughly look forward to what Rossi has in store for us readers with <i>Into the Still Blue</i>, but at the same time I'm a bit scared, and not because I'm afraid it won't be good---actually I'm absolutely positive it will be spectacular--but because it is clear through this installment that Rossi isn't afraid to put her characters through hell, and I don't even want to begin to fathom the amount tissue boxes I will inevitably go through while reading the conclusion to this stunning trilogy. Just don't hurt Roar and we'll be all good, okay? </span>
  <a data-text-id="511455034785826247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1325162038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325162038" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325162038?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=great-fighting-scenes">great-fighting-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325162038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1803291667821574248"><i>Through the Ever Night</i> is the second book in this series and the story is indeed <b>getting better</b>!<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452778530i/17741109.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The story picked up quickly after what was left in the previous book and Veronica successfully managed to create much more twists in this sequel. Those unsolved problems in the first book were perfectly answered, though she left me with even more mysteries. Luckily, we get to meet amazingly new people here, both good ones and villains. Let me start with <b>Kirra</b>, the Scire girl I <u>HATED</u> most beside Sable </span>
  <span id="freeText1803291667821574248" style="display:none"><i>Through the Ever Night</i> is the second book in this series and the story is indeed <b>getting better</b>!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452778530i/17741109.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The story picked up quickly after what was left in the previous book and Veronica successfully managed to create much more twists in this sequel. Those unsolved problems in the first book were perfectly answered, though she left me with even more mysteries. Luckily, we get to meet amazingly new people here, both good ones and villains. Let me start with <b>Kirra</b>, the Scire girl I <u>HATED</u> most beside Sable and Hess. According to the Tide and Sable’s deal, Sable promised to aid them whatever they needed so he sent Kirra and her best men to the Tide’s territory and <i>protected</i> their people. <b>Sounds pretty benevolent of him, right?</b> WRONG!!!!!!! SO WRONG ON A THOUSAND DIFFERENT LEVELS!!!!! Here what people said, <i>There’s no such thing as a free lunch.</i> Sable indeed had something to gain from the Tide, something else from what he already owned. But this was almost the end of the book, so I’ll get back to the start when Kirra met Perry. I knew her intension from the moment she showed up in front of Perry and it was rather obvious. I mean, <b>she</b> was a Scire, and so was he. <b>She</b> was curvy, beautiful, seductive, and always got whatever she wanted; in contrast, he was uncertain about himself after Aria left him abruptly. <b>She</b> could easily read his deepest thoughts and sense his temper around him, while he was easily convinced and too indecisive when his men turned out to be not that loyal to him after the chaos.---&gt; See what I’m implying? <br><blockquote>
  <b> Perry wanted to say yes. He didn’t want to be a fool who’d given his heart to a girl who’d left him. Didn’t want to feel weak anymore.<br>He didn’t answer, but Kirra came nearer anyway. Closer than she should have. He couldn’t ignore the shape of her body any longer, or the smile on her lips.</b>
</blockquote><br>Clearly, I’m making you to hate her as much as I did. (I know I’m terrible, but I just can’t stand anyone of you like/love/adore her!)<br><br>Okay, enough for the villain, let’s move on to some good and funny characters, shall we?<br>We all know that Perry became the Blood Lord of the Tide after the quick battle with his brother, Vale, in the previous book, and now he just bumped into a group of awesome fighters who happened to be somewhere in the woods in the same day he thought he’d never see Aria again. Anyway, those six men became his most loyal followers and they grew on me bit by bit. They shared some hilarious banters at times and never failed to lighten the mood in the story.<br><b>
  <blockquote>“He’s so unlucky it’s almost lucky,” Gren said. “It’s like he has reverse luck.”<br>“He’s reverse good-looking, too,” said Hyde.<br>“I’m going to reverse punch you,” Strag said to his brother.<br>“That was reverse smart, man. It means you’re going to punch yourself.”</blockquote>
</b><br>The author definitely did a great job in playing with words! That’s her writing style, though. It’s still very enjoyable for me. <br><br>Alright, back to the villain part, I’m going to introduce <i>someone</i> awfully evil and cold-blooded to you. He was the notorious Blood Lord of the Horn, <b>Sable</b>. I’ve never, ever loathed any fictional character like this and he undoubtedly crowned my all-time-despised list. Ugh. Wait until you see what he did to Liv, <b>MY BELOVED LIV</b> from the beginning of the series, or even <i>prior to</i> the main story, and I PROMISE you’ll feel me. All the rage and undeniable anger I roused at the exact moment. Simply put, this picture sums up most of my feeling. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452778530i/17741110.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Or maybe you can take a look at what I mean, but I sense the need to warn you beforehand, it hurts. Like, real hurts. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <blockquote> Her body struck the stones with a sickening thud, like a heavy sack of grain heaved to the ground. Then she lay still.</blockquote>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I suppose it’s the spell Veronica kept casting in this series. <b>
  <u>She’d make you swoon from the head all over to the toes and then back up to your head again. Then the very next minute, she’d shatter your heart into a zillion pieces that sometimes I wonder how many times it can break like this.</u>
</b> To be honest, the raw emotion was too intense to bear, let alone repeating it more than once. I didn’t feel like wailing or sobbing when those moments happened (which was weird because I think I should), but the <b>ache</b> I felt in my heart was so real. So if you want to test how strong your heart is, go ahead and read this.<br><br>After reading this book, I truly realized what the so-called <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5R4T0Nc4jig" rel="nofollow noopener">La La Land of Reality</a> was. There were way too many perfect, dreamy things that only existed in our imagination, or Aria’s. <br><b>
  <blockquote> She pictured Perry and Talon together, fishing at the end, content and relaxed. Cinder would be there too, watching them, holding his hat to keep it from blowing away. She imagined Liv and Roar nearby, whispering to each other, planning some kind of mischief that would lead, inevitably, to someone being tossed into the water. And she would be there. She’d sing something gentle and pretty. A song that would hold the sway of the waves and the warm feel of the sun. A song that would capture how she felt for all of them.</blockquote>
</b><br>Most of the time I wasn’t sure what kind of reaction or feeling should I have when dealing with these beautiful, unrealistic, not-going-to-come-true fantasies. Of course I was ecstatic and wish all the best for her along with all the good people here; it was that little gray area that blocked my vision of seeing the perfection in disguise.<br><br>As for the ending, the author once again left us with more uncertainties about what’ll really happen next so all I can say is that I’m going to find out and make a thorough exploration into the <b>
  <i>Still Blue</i>
</b>.<br><br>Lastly, here’s a quote I absolutely love in the entire book and would love to share it with all of you lovely people.<br><b>
  <blockquote> Love was like the waves in the sea, gentle and good sometimes, rough and terrible at others, but that it was endless and stronger than the sky and the earth and everything in between.</blockquote>
</b><br>**There’s a song I think it suits Aria and Perry in this book specifically due to their tough and inescapable destiny. This is <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vQM0QS8HChE" rel="nofollow noopener">Westlife-Us Against the World</a> <br><blockquote> You and I, we're been at it so long<br>But still got the strongest fire<br>You and I, we still know how to talk<br>Know how to walk that wire<br>Sometimes I feel like the world is against me<br>The sound of your voice, baby, that's what saves me<br>When we're together I feel so invincible<br>Cause it's us against the world, you and me against them all<br>If you're listening to these words know that we are standing tall<br>I don't ever see the day that I won't catch you when you fall<br>Cause it's us against the world tonight</blockquote><br>Basically, in my opinion, the entire song was perfectly made for them as if the lyrics were inspired by Aria &amp; Perry.<br><blockquote> There’ll be days we’ll be on different sides<br>But that doesn't last too long<br>We find ways to get it on track<br>And know how to turn back on<br>Sometimes I feel I can’t keep it together<br>Then you hold me close and you make it better<br>When I'm with you I can feel so unbreakable</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452778530i/17741111._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1803291667821574248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_559537470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559537470" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559537470?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=sci-fi-alicious">sci-fi-alicious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559537470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18263824406805837850">Usually V and I go on random adventures together. Like that time she was a Steampunk airship captain and I was helping her storm a flying fortress to steal back some booty. Or like when we went trekking through an alien jungle to rescue a space whale from some poachers. Ya know, we hang out. Have fun. Repress our strong feelings for each other in lieu of maintaining a platonic friendship. The usual.<br/><br/>So I’m pretty used to her taking me on wild adventures. I just don’t think I’m ever going to get u</span>
  <span id="freeText18263824406805837850" style="display:none">Usually V and I go on random adventures together. Like that time she was a Steampunk airship captain and I was helping her storm a flying fortress to steal back some booty. Or like when we went trekking through an alien jungle to rescue a space whale from some poachers. Ya know, we hang out. Have fun. Repress our strong feelings for each other in lieu of maintaining a platonic friendship. The usual.<br /><br />So I’m pretty used to her taking me on wild adventures. I just don’t think I’m ever going to get used to reading her wild imagination! Through the Ever Night was, if possible, even better than Under the Never Sky. Rossi’s skill as a story teller has only grown and improved, so too has her characters. I don’t usually like to reference character hotness as a selling point in a book – but these two don’t even need to touch to be steaming up the pages which (now that I think about it, is probably a fire hazard). As always, some of the best parts about Rossi’s writing is the litany of secondary characters – Roar being one serious MVP.<br /><br />Once again his wit and personality bring a much needed buoyancy and humour to an otherwise action-packed, edge of your seat, angst fest that left me clutching the book yelling, “What?! WHAT!?!” and “NOOOOOO!!!! NOOOO!! Oh my god howwillieversurvive!?!” You know it’s been a good book when you’re left thinking, “Oh yeah! It is ON, baby!”<br /><br />I read a lot of good books these days, having become exceptionally good at weeding out stuff I’m pretty sure I’ll like – so it takes a special kind of series/book to make my top five of all time. Under The Never Sky certainly does and not just because V would falcon punch me if I didn’t say that.<br /><br />It’s hard not to respect a book that kicks ass from start to finish. Especially the writing which has become smoother. Particularly in regards to the well-conceptualized action scenes which seems to be something that Rossi does particularly well, and everything is really easy to visualize. The Aether, an aspect of this book that exceedingly confused people the last time round, will probably still confuse you. She explains it more in this book but still, what is an Aether? Buggered if I know. And you know what? Two books in and I still don’t CARE. It’s there, it’s awesome. It’s rocking the Casbah. What’s a Casbah? I don’t know either, but it rocks. (Okay, lies. I totally know what the Casbah is. So sue me.)<br /><br />Seriously, I have a very small list of books that I love more than life itself but THIS ONE IS ON IT. Go read now!<br /><br />Because you can’t come with V and I to save the Prince from the Alturi Prison on the third moon of the Kayman system until you do!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18263824406805837850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6263095920350571488" style="display:none"><i>“Love is a rebellious bird that nobody can tame.” </i><br /><br />A great sequel to <i>Under the Never Sky</i>.<br /><br />I especially enjoyed watching Aria's relationships with Perry and Roar unfold. There was hardly any relationship drama, just a few tiny twinges of jealousy from Perry's side. But no fights and no tears. <div id="review_358980343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358980343" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358980343?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorite-book-guys">favorite-book-guys</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358980343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8516530738491743344"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382479i/740361.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><u>Give it to me</u>, she wanted to scream. <u>Give me the pain. Let me take it from you</u>.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>4.5 stars. <i>Why you hurt me, book?</i> Please forgive me for being stuck in kittah speak, but for the love of all that's good, WHY?!?<br/><br/><b>You are toying with my emotions, Ms. Rossi.</b> I don't know whether to be impressed or angry over the gut punch that I just felt. Of course, the part of me which questions everything is not going to take this lying down. I will get back up and seek out answers. I am not convinced tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8516530738491743344" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382479i/740361.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><u>Give it to me</u>, she wanted to scream. <u>Give me the pain. Let me take it from you</u>.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>4.5 stars. <i>Why you hurt me, book?</i> Please forgive me for being stuck in kittah speak, but for the love of all that's good, WHY?!?<br><br><b>You are toying with my emotions, Ms. Rossi.</b> I don't know whether to be impressed or angry over the gut punch that I just felt. Of course, the part of me which questions everything is not going to take this lying down. I will get back up and seek out answers. I am not convinced that what just happened is something that <i>actually</i> happened. At least not yet. <br><br>I'd already gone into my reasons for liking this author's writing style in my review of book 1, but a lot of my initial impressions have stayed pretty much the same. If you're looking for heavily detailed sci-fi and explicit world building, you're not going to find it in this series. These books are completely character driven.<br><br>Needless to say, I did find myself somewhat surprised at how little of a part the 'realms' played into TTEN. By this point, I'm not sure how much description we're ever going to get on that side of the coin. Should this bother me? I don't know. Maybe? For whatever reason that makes no sense to me, I'm somehow <i>happy</i> with the world outside of the realms and the stories and interactions happening on the side of the coin we're staring at.<br><br>My poor heart was overwhelmed for most of this book. This isn't to say that everything was going wrong. In fact, I had so many warm fuzzies when it came to the bond between Aria and Roar. How often do you see a strong friendship portrayed between a male and female in which the reward is simply the friendship itself?<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> (Yes, but this feels intimate. Don't you think it does? Roar, sometimes it's hard to get used to this.)<br>Roar flashed a grin, "Aria, this isn't intimate. If I were being intimate with you, trust me, you'd know."<br>They fell into silence, and she realized how comforting it felt being connected to someone this way.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>The romances in the story are absolutely rewarding in and of themselves (Aria and Perry are still flipping adorable), but in this particular installment, I was surprised to find myself caught up in Aria and Roar's journey as friends who were there for each other through their darkest nights. Their friendly, teasing banter and shared commonality evolved into something deeper, something pure.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Roar slept with a soft smile on his lips. His skin was a shade too pale. She memorized the way he looked. Aria wasn't sure when she'd see him smile again.<br>He was beautiful, and it wasn't fair.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Perry was different in this book, but in a good way. He'd matured, now that he has more responsibility on his shoulders. I still love him to pieces, and am looking forward to his place in the bigger picture of this story. <br><br>Even with the subtle and sparse world building, the writing style is still lush and descriptive. I am not sure how to get an explanation across clearly, since the previous sentence sort of contradicts itself. The characters are still shining, the relationships continue to make me feel, the adventures are fun, and the wording managed to make me tear up a few times. This author writes in such a way that I find myself stopping to re-read certain paragraphs just because I love what was written.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Aria smiled at what he'd said. He didn't know why, but it didn't matter. She was smiling.<br><br>Perry brushed her hair away from her shoulder and breathed her in, letting the strength of her temper bring him back. One breath at a time, his anger faded into desire.<br><br>She sang a song he knew this time - one she'd sung to him when they'd been at Marron's together. It was a message from her. A reminder - here among hundreds of people - of a moment that had been theirs alone.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes, the story is one I enjoy. Yes, there is an interesting virtual reality aspect happening. Yes, there are adventures and danger to be had. Yes, there is more to all of <i>this</i> world than just emotions and lovely characters. But I can only write about what the book meant to me. And for me, every shining moment came from character interaction. It was not the fight scenes, nor the chasing after people, nor the mystery of what isn't being told. What works for me is what is peeking out from the layers of story...it's those little flashes of light which have me transfixed and longing for the next book.<br><br><i>This book provided from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><br>Are you an adult who is still young at heart? Come share your passion for YA fic with us! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/51118" rel="nofollow noopener">Rated YA-MA</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_482206529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482206529" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482206529?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781907411069" href="/book/show/14742334-through-the-ever-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=open-ending">open-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=atom">atom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=creepy-love-triangle">creepy-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482206529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9305339402761350129">It's not often that a sequel outshines its predecessor, but with Through the Ever Night, it seems to be the general consensus. We've had a few examples here and there, and they've all proved to be pretty memorable, but I don't think I've ever seen a case quite like this. Don't get me wrong – I loved Under the Never Sky, it was fresh and dynamical and it left a lasting impression, but due to its intensity, Through the Ever Night is far more remarkable. Rossi has grown more confident as a writer, </span>
  <span id="freeText9305339402761350129" style="display:none">It's not often that a sequel outshines its predecessor, but with Through the Ever Night, it seems to be the general consensus. We've had a few examples here and there, and they've all proved to be pretty memorable, but I don't think I've ever seen a case quite like this. Don't get me wrong – I loved Under the Never Sky, it was fresh and dynamical and it left a lasting impression, but due to its intensity, Through the Ever Night is far more remarkable. Rossi has grown more confident as a writer, the success of her debut has done her a world of good, and her newly found self-assurance shines from every page. As with everything else, the attitude makes so much difference, it's a well-known fact, and Rossi now firmly stands on her own two feet. I believe we can expect great things from her.<br><br>I deem it necessary to mention that the book is perfectly paced. Like its predecessor, it’s told from both Aria and Perry’s point of view, and while third person alternating view is by far my least favorite narrative mode, Rossi made it work splendidly. I can’t imagine Through the Ever Night told any other way. <br><br>It goes without saying that things never go smoothly for Perry and Aria. Theirs is a romance I’m very fond of and left to their own devices, they would be no more than a step away from their happily ever after. However, there’s not one, but two worlds between them: Aria’s Dwellers would never accept someone like Peregrine, a savage by their standards, and his Tides have nothing but insults for Aria, with only a few exceptions. <br><br>Even though their feelings for each other were constantly being put to the test, through it all, they both grew tremendously as individuals. Aria is nothing like that pale, scared girl from Under the Never Sky. She is confident, fierce, a strong Aud and a good friend. All her attitudes and prejudices are gone. There is both strength and grace in her gait she didn’t possess before, and she certainly knows what to do with a knife. But there are also changes on the inside, she cares for people differently and she values different things.<br><i>
  <b>She’d been seeking the comfort of a place. Of walls. A roof. A pillow to rest her head on. Now she realized that the people she loved were what gave her life shape, and comfort, and meaning. Perry and Roar were home.</b>
</i><br><br>Changes on Perry are perhaps less evident, but they are just as big. Through his responsibility toward his tribe and more losses than he can count, he gained a somber maturity that he lacked before. His every step, every single word carries more weight, and each decision he makes shapes the lives of many. He is a far cry from that rash, headstrong boy we know from Under the Never Sky, and if I had to choose one thing that really stood out in this book, it would be his characterization – the subtle changes found between the lines, but perhaps more important for the remainder of the story than everything else put together.<br><br>There are things in Through the Ever Night that will make you laugh, things that will make you cry, things that will make you inch up nervously in your seat, some that will make you angry enough to punch something (hopefully not someone, though), and things that will make you swoon. Now, aren’t those signs of a perfect read?<br><br>I think you’ve all noticed that my five star ratings are few and far between, but a book that had… HAS such a tight hold on my heart, that still lingers in my mind even though it’s been weeks since I’d finished it, definitely deserves my wholehearted support. Veronica Rossi does, too. While the ending was open, but entirely satisfactory, Into the Still Blue can’t come soon enough, I tell you. I will be right here, nervously biting my nails until it does. <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9305339402761350129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_491136896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491136896" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491136896?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491136896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7832126410790799117"><b>Through the Ever Night</b> was AMAZING! Everything I loved about Under the Never Sky was kicked up several notches and then some! Epic adventure, heart-pounding action, romance, friendship, longing, and heartbreak are all found within the pages. I’m still reeling with awe at the love I have for this story! <br/><br/>We pick up right where the story left off in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10756656.Under_the_Never_Sky__Under_the_Never_Sky___1_' title='Under the Never Sky (Under the Never Sky, #1) by Veronica Rossi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under the Never Sky</a> where Aria and Perry meet again. Their love for each other is strong, but they face so many outside challenges. The Aether storms s</span>
  <span id="freeText7832126410790799117" style="display:none"><b>Through the Ever Night</b> was AMAZING! Everything I loved about Under the Never Sky was kicked up several notches and then some! Epic adventure, heart-pounding action, romance, friendship, longing, and heartbreak are all found within the pages. I’m still reeling with awe at the love I have for this story! <br /><br />We pick up right where the story left off in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10756656.Under_the_Never_Sky__Under_the_Never_Sky___1_" title="Under the Never Sky (Under the Never Sky, #1) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Never Sky</a> where Aria and Perry meet again. Their love for each other is strong, but they face so many outside challenges. The Aether storms seem to be growing both in frequency and intensity, so all the tribes and even the Realms need to find a safe haven before everything necessary for life is destroyed. Aria is tasked with the mission to find the elusive Still Blue, an area that is supposed to be unharmed by the Aether storms, by Consul Hess. He’s blackmailed her into cooperating or risk the well-being of Talon, Perry’s beloved nephew. Perry is now Blood Lord to the Tides but all is not smooth sailing. The decision to bring Aria back to the Tides is met with suspicion, and most of the Tides members hate her even if she is half Outsider. The Tides don’t fully trust Perry either, questioning his decisions as their leader, and Perry feels their doubt profoundly. <br /><br />Oh man, was this good! I loved <b>Under the Never Sky</b> but I think this surpasses that story, something almost unheard of with a sequel. No dreaded “second book syndrome” where much of the story is filler, gearing up for the final wrap-up in the last book. This story was thrilling in every way and almost impossible to put down. <br /><br />I loved the romance between Perry and Aria. Their characters are so well fleshed out, and you feel their concerns, despair, joy, and love right along with them. They are from two different worlds but their care and love for the people around them, and their common goals make them well-suited for each other. They had to weather a few storms, and I think they’ve become stronger for it. I love this quote:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Her eyes blurred, and she wasn’t sure if it was from the pain or from the relief of being with him again. He brought a sense of rightness. She felt it every moment she spent with him. Even the wrong ones. Even the painful ones, like now. Perry’s hands stilled. He looked up, and his gaze told her everything. He felt it too.*</i>
</b><br /><br />Secondary character such as Roar and Cinder, and even Soren add layers to an already amazing tale, and I found myself fully invested in their stories, as well. This was an exciting adventure, filled with action, and danger. Where we leave off in this installment has me anxious and super eager for the conclusion. I really like the way things are shaping up, and I think the next story has real potential to be just as exciting as this one. Veronica Rossi has managed to stun an amaze me, and I can’t wait to pick up her next book! <br /><br /><i>*Quote taken from an uncorrected proof and may change in the final copy.<br /><br />A copy was provided by HarperCollins through Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. Thank you. </i> <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7832126410790799117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1692012803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692012803" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1692012803?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781907411069" href="/book/show/14742334-through-the-ever-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692012803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13594653842896904847"><b>"We lose and lose, but we're still here."</b><br/><br/>•I never expected this to be a major issue in this review, but I can't deny it kept my mind occupied far more than I'd liked: <b>the romance</b>. All things considered, I can only describe it as <b>miserably sickly-sweet</b>. In <i>Through The Ever Night</i>, as main hobby <b>everyone whines, mopes, moans, gets so edgy</b> that the only plausible explanation is that they're all on their period (men included) and I swear, <i>I swear</i>, if I could have slapped the lovebirds myself, I would</span>
  <span id="freeText13594653842896904847" style="display:none"><b>"We lose and lose, but we're still here."</b><br /><br />•I never expected this to be a major issue in this review, but I can't deny it kept my mind occupied far more than I'd liked: <b>the romance</b>. All things considered, I can only describe it as <b>miserably sickly-sweet</b>. In <i>Through The Ever Night</i>, as main hobby <b>everyone whines, mopes, moans, gets so edgy</b> that the only plausible explanation is that they're all on their period (men included) and I swear, <i>I swear</i>, if I could have slapped the lovebirds myself, I would have. Violently. Not only once. Seriously, people, <b>you should all get your priorities straight</b>. The world is dying etc. etc., and the first thing on your mind is that you can't see each other for a few weeks? What about throwing your responsibilities out of the window, digging a hole all to yourselves and getting it over with? And it's not only that this infuriating tendecy to complain about their nothings makes their characters appear twice as <b>spineless</b> as they actually are (or should be), it's also that it makes me feel as though the book weren't worth reading, because sorry if I feel let down when I choose to read a sci-fi story and end up with two characters whose main (and cumbersome) concern is their not being together (for perfectly valid reasons, by the way, but it seems that if you're in love your brain is allowed to go on vacation).<br /><br />•<b>Aria's and Roar's frindship</b> is something remarkable indeed. I don't think I ever stumbled upon a platonic relationship between a boy and a girl that touched me so. <br /><br />•<b>The writing</b>, sadly, is still rather <b>average</b>. I am well aware that this is the very adjective I used in my review of <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1612203887?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Under The Never Sky</a>,</i> and I apologize for my lack of originality in this regard. I am afraid I am answering to mediocrity and blandness with blandness and mediocrity.<br /><br />•Now this is awkward, because I've only spoken a little about the romance and the writing, without even going into detail nor analyzing the characters one by one as I usually do, and <b>I already have nothing more to say</b>. I am sorry if you'll find this review less exhaustive than usual (that is, if you usually find my reviews decently exhaustive, which I have not the arrogance to believe), but the only word that comes to my mind is, again, <b>average</b>. <b>Average</b>, <b>average</b>, <b>average</b>. It's <b>easy to read</b> and <b>entertaining</b>, and those are perks I can't in any way ignore, but besides that, there's very little to save.<br /><br />➽ I hoped in an improvement on the first book, which, in all fairness, was not half bad to begin with, but I think it legit to expect something more from the second installment, be it a trilogy or a longer series. Therefore, <b>generally speaking, I am disappointed</b>. Still, I don't lose all hope for the conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13594653842896904847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1298226276" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1298226276" />
    <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela"><img alt="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487543962p2/28640648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1298226276?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela">Melissa (Ever So Mela)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1298226276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13739726309702867518">3.5<br/><b>Will these books ever cease to surprise me?!?!?<br/>This is the <u>second</u> book in a trilogy.</b><br/><u>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I.DID.NOT.HATE.IT!</blockquote>
  </i>
</u><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433462692ra/15099616.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just...I...<i>what?</i><br/><br/>This series has honestly surprised me to no end. I'm very wary when I go into second books from a trilogy, like, I go with the lowest expectations because I know they're bound to be slow, I know nothing really happens and always tend to expect the worst (even though the worst still manages to piss me off). So going into this book and coming out as happy as I did.</span>
  <span id="freeText13739726309702867518" style="display:none">3.5<br><b>Will these books ever cease to surprise me?!?!?<br>This is the <u>second</u> book in a trilogy.</b><br><u>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I.DID.NOT.HATE.IT!</blockquote>
  </i>
</u><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433462692ra/15099616.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just...I...<i>what?</i><br><br>This series has honestly surprised me to no end. I'm very wary when I go into second books from a trilogy, like, I go with the lowest expectations because I know they're bound to be slow, I know nothing really happens and always tend to expect the worst (even though the worst still manages to piss me off). So going into this book and coming out as happy as I did. Look, I'm just <b>ridiculously thankful.</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433464489ra/15099738.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously Rossi, <i>thank you</i>.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Love was like the waves in the sea, gentle and good sometimes, rough and terrible at others, but that it was endless and stronger than the sky and earth and everything in between.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>This book is heartfelt. You can practically taste the love these characters have. And I'm not talking about the love between Aria and Parry. I mean in every other character. You see it in the way Roar aches for Liv, in the way Perry defends his tribe, in the way Aria fights for what's right. You hear it in their words and see it in their actions. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433464489ra/15099739.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I adore these characters! I've probably mentioned it already and you know what? I don't care. <b>I love these characters!</b> They are what bring these books alive. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Roar's smile widened. "I know. You missed me." <br>She rolled her eyes. "It's barely been three weeks since I last saw you."<br>"Miserable stretch of time." He said.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I adore Roar and the fact that the author brought a male to the story without the possibility of there being a triangle. He's a constant in her life, her rock, her safe place. I'm fascinated by their loyalty to each other and to the dynamic rumble they bring to the story. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We lose and lose, but we're still here. Shaking in place, afraid of doing something. I'm tired of settling for this because I don't know if something better exists. It has to. What point is there otherwise? I can do something about it now. And I will.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>This was a suspenseful, action packed, edge of your seat kind of story that had me biting my nails from the stress. What I loved most what the realness it portrayed which we don't really see a lot of in YA. It's not always going to be perfect and they won't always win and Rossi manged that flawlessly. I mean this woman had me scared of turning to the next page never knowing what was going to happen. Seriously Rossi, I'm going to repeat myself. <i>Thank you!</i><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Love is a rebellious bird that nobody can tame.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422397909i/13498279.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13739726309702867518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_338166078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338166078" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338166078?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=rainy-day-re-reads">rainy-day-re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338166078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13134487306796128002">Rating: 4.5 Stars <br/><br/><i>Through the Ever Night</i> is one of the few sequels that truly took me by surprise - in the best possible way. I can't quite articulate how excited I was for this book, especially after loving <i>Under the Never Sky,</i> so to say that my expectations were met would be an understatement. Once again, Veronica Rossi has proved her prowess as a writer and if there's anything I can guarantee, it's that fans of the series will most definitely <i>not</i> be disappointed by this scintillating sequel.<br/><br/><i>T</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13134487306796128002" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5 Stars <br /><br /><i>Through the Ever Night</i> is one of the few sequels that truly took me by surprise - in the best possible way. I can't quite articulate how excited I was for this book, especially after loving <i>Under the Never Sky,</i> so to say that my expectations were met would be an understatement. Once again, Veronica Rossi has proved her prowess as a writer and if there's anything I can guarantee, it's that fans of the series will most definitely <i>not</i> be disappointed by this scintillating sequel.<br /><br /><i>Through the Ever Night</i> picks up exactly where <i>Under the Never Sky</i> left off with the reunion of Aria and Perry. Unlike its predecessor, which was rather fast-paced and full of romance, <i>Through the Ever Night</i> is filled with a steady undercurrent of loss, of longing, and an atmosphere of tension. Even from the beginning, we can see that this won't be the same swoon-worthy romance we were treated to in the first novel. Instead, Aria and Perry are practically estranged from one another as Aria is very much an outsider in Perry's tribe and their relationship is kept a secret. Yet, before Perry and Aria can even begin to come to terms with the direction their relationship is taking now that they are no longer alone, Aria and Roar are whisked away to find Liv, Perry's sister, and fulfill the task of finding the Still Blue.<br /><br />It seems weird, but for some reason, I always enjoy romances that are tinged with a hint of longing, despair, and utter <i>want,</i> which was exactly what I got with <i>Through the Ever Night.</i> Even while living in the same tribe, Aria and Perry seem miles away from one another, until literally, they are. As Blood Lord of the Tides, Perry has an immense amount of responsibility, and it doesn't all come so easily. It is evident that as a leader, the role one plays is extremely different and seeing Perry struggle through his duty, making mistakes and blunders, all while slowly coming to realize his significance and grow into his role, is an incredible journey to see. Just like with her debut, Rossi manages to capture the essence of humanity within her characters, making them shockingly three-dimensional and realistic in the growth and change that she ensures they go through throughout the novel.<br /><br />Aria, too, is a different person. Although we don't see as drastic a change of growth in her as we do in Perry, she is a far cry from the frightened Dweller we met in the beginning of <i>Under the Never Sky.</i> Aria and Roar's friendship is as strong as ever and seeing them interact, console each other, and just generally be there for one another without any romantic feelings on part of either of them was utterly refreshing. I love that Rossi made Aria just as much a friend to Roar as Perry and furthermore, that she made Roar such a huge forefront in this novel. Although he doesn't have his own PoV in this novel, like Aria and Perry do, a large part of the plot revolves around him and seeing <i>him</i> change and grow is rewarding as well.<br /><br />In addition to the main characters, the majority of the secondary characters from <i>Under the Never Sky</i> return in this novel, some of them in unexpected ways. I was thrilled to see them all come back and see the role they played in moving the plot forward. If I have any qualms with this story, it is just that it seems as if not enough quite happens. It almost seems as if there is still <i>so much</i> left to happen in the last novel, but the plot never lags, never slows, and never bores the reader. It isn't as fast-paced or intriguing as <i>Under the Never Sky,</i> and many of my questions concerning Aria's parentage remain unanswered, but it keeps you flipping the pages and the world-building is explored a little further as well.<br /><br />Ultimately, I can see this novel being an instant hit with fans of <i>Under the Never Sky</i> for it is a fabulous follow-up novel. Veronica Rossi just keeps surprising me. While <em>Under the Never Sky</em> felt like Aria's story, TtEN is Perry's in a way and it's phenomenal. I simply love the character development in this novel. It completely blew me away with its depth. COMPLETELY. Furthermore, it was an <i>incredibly</i> emotional novel. INCREDIBLY. Seriously, my feelings and emotions were EVERYWHERE. It was an incredible whirlwind of pure emotion for sure. If there is anything I know for sure it is that <em>Into the Still Blue</em> is going to be SUCH a great conclusion - I can just tell. <br /><br /><i>HUGE hugs and kisses and thank-yous to my friend, Amelia, at <a href="http://theauthoress-amelia.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Authoress</a> for lending me this book. You're the BEST, Amelia! THANK YOU!&lt;3 </i> <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/01/arc-review-through-ever-night-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13134487306796128002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_384481925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384481925" />
    <a title="Anja H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h"><img alt="Anja H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559051853p2/6054186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384481925?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384481925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12643394803229116550"><b>*4.5 EPIC STARS*</b><br/><br/>It's been 2 years since I read the first book in this series, but I rolled right back into this story like I never stopped reading! Perry and Aria's adventure is just so fast-paced and exciting, it <b>never</b> gets boring.<br/>Though I don't remember absolutely everything about the first book, it was pretty easy to get back into this. Perry and Aria are both unique and unforgettable characters who care deeply for each other and it really shows throughout the whole story. <br/>I really like the w</span>
  <span id="freeText12643394803229116550" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 EPIC STARS*</b><br /><br />It's been 2 years since I read the first book in this series, but I rolled right back into this story like I never stopped reading! Perry and Aria's adventure is just so fast-paced and exciting, it <b>never</b> gets boring.<br />Though I don't remember absolutely everything about the first book, it was pretty easy to get back into this. Perry and Aria are both unique and unforgettable characters who care deeply for each other and it really shows throughout the whole story. <br />I really like the way this book is told: alternating between both Aria's and Perry's perspectives. (I don't remember whether it was also like that in the first book.) <br />Even though they were apart most of the time, they constantly thought about each other so you never had to miss either one of them for very long. It was interesting to read what the one was up to while certain things happened to the other. They both struggled through their own hardships throughout the story but emerged even stronger and more in love than before!<br />This book also contained a lot of Roar... <i>Oh Roar, how I love you!</i>. Don't get me wrong, I love Perry, but I really have a soft spot for Roar! I'm glad Aria's and Roar's relationship stayed platonic though, I wouldn't have it any other way.<br />The one thing I didn't like was that the book was a bit <b>too</b> fast-paced in my opinion, at times I felt that the story could have been a bit more elaborate instead of going from one action-packed scene to the next! It all felt a bit rushed and hectic to me. I could've done with a slower pace!<br />Overall, I really enjoyed this and I already started the last book! Can't wait to see how they're gonna wrap things up in just one more book! <b>Bring it on!</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12643394803229116550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
